<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="baby-resuscitation">Baby resuscitation:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#baby-resuscitation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="danger">Danger<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#danger" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Make sure you are safe to help, do not put yourself in danger</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="response">Response<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#response" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Gently tap the baby’s shoulders and shout to try to wake the baby</li>
<li>If the baby does not respond shout for help, but don’t leave the baby yet</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="airway">Airway<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#airway" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Carefully ensure the airway is open by gently tipping the baby’s head back with the ‘chin lift’:</p>
<ul>
<li>Place your hand on the baby’s forehead and gently tilt their head back. DO NOT OVER-EXTEND THE BABY’S NECK</li>
<li>Using your fingertips under the point of the chin, lift the chin to open the airway</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="breathing">Breathing<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#breathing" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Ensuring the airway is kept open; look, listen and feel to ascertain whether the baby is breathing normally. Do not take more than ten seconds to do this.</p>
<ul>
<li>If the baby is able to breath normally, consider the baby’s injuries and place them in the recovery position (see page 12)</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251222-37d7f3e1.jpeg" alt="img-23.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="if-the-baby-is-not-breathing-normally">If the baby is not breathing normally:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#if-the-baby-is-not-breathing-normally" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>If you are not alone, ask the nearest person to dial 999 for an ambulance immediately. If you are alone and need to leave the baby to ensure help is on the way, perform resuscitation for about 1 minute first:</li>
<li>Maintain the baby’s airway by tilting their head and lifting the chin ensuring you do not over-extend the baby’s neck</li>
<li>Seal your mouth around the baby’s nose and mouth</li>
<li>Give 5 initial rescue breaths. Blow in just enough air to make the baby’s chest rise visibly. Be careful not to over inflate the baby’s lungs</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="combine-rescue-breaths-with-chest-compressions">Combine rescue breaths with chest compressions:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#combine-rescue-breaths-with-chest-compressions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Use 2 fingers to depress the baby’s chest to a third of its depth</li>
<li>Give 30 chest compressions at a rate of 100 compressions per minute</li>
<li>Open the airway again by tilting the baby’s head and lifting the chin, and give 2 more rescue breaths</li>
<li>Continue to administer 30 chest compressions followed by 2 rescue breaths</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>If your rescue breaths do not make the baby’s chest rise effectively:</p>
<p>Give a further 30 chest compressions before attempting the following:</p>
<ul>
<li>Check inside the mouth and remove any clearly visible obstruction (do not reach blindly into the baby’s throat)</li>
<li>Recheck that the head is adequately tilted back and the chin is lifted</li>
<li>Do not administer more than 2 rescue breaths before resuming chest compressions</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="appendix-resuscitation-with-an-automated-external-defibrillator-aed">Appendix: Resuscitation with an Automated External Defibrillator (AED):<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#appendix-resuscitation-with-an-automated-external-defibrillator-aed" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The most common cause of a heart stopping (cardiac arrest) is a ‘heart attack’ (see page 30). It is worth noting that a heart attack does not always result in cardiac arrest. The majority of heart attack victims remain conscious and survive.</p>
<p>If a heart attack, or another cause, results in cardiac arrest, it is usually because it has interrupted the heart’s electrical impulses. When this happens the heart ‘quivers’ chaotically instead of beating in the usual co-ordinated rhythm. This is known as ‘Ventricular Fibrillation’ (VF).</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251222-57c5da5e.jpeg" alt="img-24.jpeg">
Normal Sinus Rhythm</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251222-11e68136.jpeg" alt="img-25.jpeg">
Ventricular Fibrillation</p>
<p>The definitive treatment for ventricular fibrillation is to administer a controlled electric shock to the heart, which stops the ‘quiver’ and enables it to start beating normally again. This treatment is called ‘defibrillation’.</p>
<p>An Automated External Defibrillator (AED) is a safe and reliable computerised device that analyses the heart rhythms and enables a non-medically qualified person to safely administer the life-saving shock, with some small amount of training.</p>
<p>Using an AED can drastically increase the chances of a casualty’s survival if their heart stops beating, but prompt use is paramount. For every minute’s delay in delivering the shock, the casualty’s chance of survival is reduced by 10%.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="resuscitation-with-an-aed">Resuscitation with an AED<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#resuscitation-with-an-aed" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="danger">Danger<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#danger" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Make sure you are safe to help, do not put yourself in danger</li>
<li>Consider the safety implications of using an AED in this situation</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="response">Response<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#response" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Gently shake the shoulders and ask in a loud voice ‘Are you alright?’ If there is no response from the casualty:</li>
<li>Shout for help immediately</li>
<li>If you have people with you, ask one helper to dial 999 for an ambulance and ask the other to get the AED, but do not leave the casualty yourself just yet</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="airway">Airway<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#airway" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Carefully ensure the airway is open by gently tipping the head back lifting the chin</li>
</ul>
<p>This document is available on

studocu

Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="breathing">Breathing<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#breathing" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Ensuring the airway is kept open; look, listen and feel to ascertain whether the casualty is breathing normally. Do not take more than ten seconds to do this.</p>
<ul>
<li>If the casualty is able to breath <strong>normally</strong>, consider possible injuries and carefully place them in the recovery position (see page 12)</li>
</ul>
<p>If the casualty is not breathing normally:</p>
<ul>
<li>If you are alone, <strong>dial 999</strong> for an ambulance and <strong>get the AED</strong> – you may have to leave the casualty to do this</li>
<li>If you have people with you, start CPR immediately while one helper <strong>dials 999</strong> for an ambulance and the other helper <strong>gets the AED</strong>. Continue CPR yourself until the AED arrives</li>
</ul>
<p>When the AED arrives:</p>
<ul>
<li>If you have someone helping you ask them to take over CPR while you get the AED ready.
NOTE: If the person with you is untrained in CPR it may be easier for them to administer the chest Compressions only (see page 4).</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="switch-on-the-aed-immediately-and-follow-the-voice-prompts">Switch on the AED immediately and follow the voice prompts:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#switch-on-the-aed-immediately-and-follow-the-voice-prompts" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Attach the leads to the AED if they are not already attached, and attach the pads to the casualty’s bare chest (if possible, do this while the person helping you continues CPR)</li>
<li>It may be necessary for you to towel dry or even shave the casualty’s chest so the pads adhere to their skin properly. Only shave where the pads are going to go, try to delay defibrillation as little as possible</li>
<li>Peel the backing from the pads one at a time and place them firmly in position, following the instruction on the pads</li>
<li>Place the first pad below the casualty’s right collar bone</li>
<li>Place the second pad on the casualty’s left side, over the lower ribs. Try to place the second pad vertically if possible.</li>
</ul>
<p>DO NOT REMOVE THE PADS ONCE YOU HAVE PLACED THEM IF THEY ARE THE WRONG WAY ROUND – THE AED WILL STILL WORK.</p>
<p>Wait while the AED analyses the casualty’s heart rhythm – stop CPR while this happens and ensure no one touches the casualty</p>
<p>If the AED advises a shock:</p>
<ul>
<li>Ensure no one is touching the casualty (check from top to toe and clearly shout ‘stand clear!’)</li>
<li>Push the shock button when prompted (if the AED is fully automated it will deliver the shock automatically)</li>
<li>Continue as directed by the voice or visual prompts from the AED</li>
</ul>
<p>If the AED does not advise a shock:</p>
<ul>
<li>Immediately resume CPR using the ratio of 30 chest compressions to 2 rescue breaths</li>
<li>Continue as directed by the voice or visual prompts from the AED</li>
</ul>
<p>Page | 81</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="placements-of-the-pads">Placements of the pads:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#placements-of-the-pads" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="wet-chest">Wet chest<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#wet-chest" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>If the casualty’s chest is wet (from sweating for example) it must be dried before the pads can be applied so they can stick to the skin properly. Also be sure to dry the area of the chest between the pads, as electricity can ‘arc’ across the wet skin.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="excessive-chest-hair">Excessive chest hair<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#excessive-chest-hair" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Hair on the chest will stop the pads from sticking to the skin properly and will interfere with electrical contact. You only need to shave the chest if the hair is excessive, and even then take as little time as possible as you don’t want to delay defibrillation by any longer than is absolutely necessary. If there is no razor immediately available, do not delay defibrillation.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="pad-positioning">Pad positioning<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pad-positioning" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Research shows that the position of the pad on the lower left side of the chest has an impact on the effectiveness of the shock. When placing the pad, make sure it is placed around the side of the chest (not on the front) and place it vertically. This will help ensure the maximum electricity flows through the heart rather than across the surface of the chest. If the AED has not been updated, the pads will have a diagram showing horizontal placement – ignore this advice and place the pad vertically.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="aed-safety-considerations">AED safety considerations:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#aed-safety-considerations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="electric-shock">Electric shock<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#electric-shock" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Studies have shown that, providing the pads are stuck to a dry chest in the correct positions, the risk of electrical shock is very low as the electricity wants to travel from one pad to the other, not to ‘earth’ itself like mains electricity. However, to be on the safe side, always briefly check that no one is touching the casualty before a shock is delivered.</p>
<p><strong>DO NOT delay defibrillation because the casualty is lying on a wet or metal surface, providing the chest area is dry it is safe to administer the shock.</strong></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="medication-patches">Medication patches<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#medication-patches" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Some casualties will wear a patch to administer their medication (e.g. a nicotine patch). Some heart patients wear a ‘glyceryl tri-nitrate’ (GTN) patch. Please be aware that this type of patch can explode if electricity is passed through it. Remove any visible medication patches before administering a shock as a precaution.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="jewellery">Jewellery<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#jewellery" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Be aware when placing the pads that you do not place them on any jewellery, such as a necklace. This would conduct the electricity and burn the casualty. There is no need to remove any piercings, but avoid placing the pads over any.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="implanted-devices">Implanted devices<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#implanted-devices" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Some heart patients have pacemakers or defibrillator implants. These can usually be seen or felt under the skin when the chest is exposed, there may also be a scar. The implants are usually situated just below the left collar bone and should not be in the way of the AED pad. However, if the device has been implanted elsewhere, try not to place the pad directly over it.</p>
<p>This document is available on
studocu
Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>Page | 82</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>Highly flammable atmosphere</p>
<p>As with any electrical equipment, there is a possibility of the AED creating a spark when the shock is administered, so it should not be used in a highly flammable atmosphere (in the presence of a gas leak for example).</p>
<p>Inappropriate shock</p>
<p>AED machines have been proven to analyse the heart’s rhythm extremely accurately. However, the casualty needs to be motionless while the AED does the analysis. You must not use an AED on a casualty who is fitting (violent, jerking movements), and ensure vehicle engines or vibrating machines are switched off wherever possible.</p>
<p>AED use on children:</p>
<p>The AED pads are suitable for both adults and children older than 8 years. Smaller pads that reduce the current delivered in a shock are available for children aged 1 to 8 years. These should be used for the appropriate age range whenever possible. Some AEDs have a ‘paediatric’ setting.</p>
<p>If the child is over 1 year and you do not have smaller pads, use the AED as it is. But please note that the use of adult sized pads on a child under 1 year old is not recommended.</p>
<p>Most paediatric pads are designed to be placed with one in the centre of the child’s chest and the other in the centre of the child’s back. The pads should have a diagram showing their correct positions.</p>
<p>Some paediatric pads are designed to be placed in the same position as the adult pads – always follow the diagrams on the pads to ensure you are placing them in the correct place.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="glossary">Glossary<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#glossary" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Abdomen
the area between the lowest ribs and the pelvis</p>
<p>Acute
sudden onset</p>
<p>Adrenaline
Hormone secreted by the body in times of shock</p>
<p>Airway
the passage from the mouth and nose to the lungs</p>
<p>Alveoli
minute air sacks in the lungs, through which the exchange of gasses take place</p>
<p>Asphyxia
deficiency of oxygen caused by an interruption in the passage of air to the lungs</p>
<p>Atrium
top, ‘collecting’ chamber of the heart (of which there are two)</p>
<p>Baby
person under 1 year old</p>
<p>Breathing
inspiration and expiration of air into and out of the lungs</p>
<p>Bronchioles
small air passages in the lungs, leading to the alveoli</p>
<p>Cardiac / cardiogenic
concerned with the heart</p>
<p>Cell
smallest structural living unit of an organism</p>
<p>Cerebral-spinal fluid (CSF)
fluid that surrounds the brain and spinal cord, to cushion it and provide nutrients</p>
<p>Cerebrum
the largest part of the brain</p>
<p>Cervical
concerned with the neck</p>
<p>Child
person between 1 year old and puberty</p>
<p>Chronic
long term</p>
<p>Circulation
the movement of blood around the body</p>
<p>Compression
bleeding or swelling in the cranial cavity, exerting pressure on the brain</p>
<p>Concussion
shaking of the brain, causing temporary loss of consciousness or function</p>
<p>Consciousness
alertness, ‘normal’ activity of the brain</p>
<p>Constrict
to close down, become narrower</p>
<p>Convulsion
fit or seizure</p>
<p>CPR
Cardio Pulmonary Resuscitation, manually squeezing the heart and breathing for a casualty</p>
<p>Cranium
the cavity in the skull in which the brain lies</p>
<p>Cyanosis
blue/grey tinges to the skin, especially the lips, due to lack of oxygen</p>
<p>Defibrillation
the delivery of a large electric shock to the chest in an attempt to re-start the heart</p>
<p>Dilate
become wider, open up</p>
<p>Enzyme
substance that enables a biological reaction to happen</p>
<p>Epistaxis
nose bleed</p>
<p>Face shield
protective mask with a one-way valve for performing mouth-to-mouth rescue breaths</p>
<p>Febrile
relating to fever or high body temperature</p>
<p>Haemothorax
bleeding into the pleural cavity of the lungs</p>
<p>Hepatic
relating to the liver</p>
<p>Hyper...
high</p>
<p>Hypo...
low</p>
<p>Hypothalamus
area of the brain that controls the body’s temperature</p>
<p>Hypovolaemic
low volume of blood, a type of shock</p>
<p>Hypoxia
low levels of oxygen in the blood</p>
